envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n7: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\\\";\\n8: import \\\"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\\\";\\n9: import \\\"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\\\";\\n10: \\n11: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n12: import \\\"google/protobuf/struct.proto\\\";\\n13: \\n14: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n15: import \\\"validate/validate.proto\\\";\\n16: \\n17: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\\\";\\n18: option java_outer_classname = \\\"ExtProcProto\\\";\\n19: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n20: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n21: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n22: \\n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n24: // External Processing Filter\\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n26: \\n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n91: // server\\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n95: //\\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n98: // name.\\n99: //\\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\\n102:   reserved 4;\\n103: \\n104:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n105: \\n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n107:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n109: \\n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n118: \\n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\\n122: \\n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\\n129: \\n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\\n136: \\n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n21: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n22: \\n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n24: // External Processing Filter\\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n26: \\n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n91: // server\\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n95: //\\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n98: // name.\\n99: //\\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\\n102:   reserved 4;\\n103: \\n104:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n105: \\n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n107:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n109: \\n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n118: \\n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n120:   // sent. syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n8: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n9: import \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n10: \n11: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n12: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n15: (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n22: \n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n24: // External Processing Filter\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n26: \n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n28: \n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n31: //\n32: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n33: \n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n36: //\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n41: //\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n44: // and how it should be processed.\n45: //\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n47: //\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n53: //\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\n57: //\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n63: //   to SEND.\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n69: //   request trailers.\n70: //\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n78: //\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n81: //\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n89: //\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n91: // server\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n95: //\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n98: // name.\n99: //\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\n102:   reserved 4;\n103: \n104:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n105: \n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n107:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n109: \n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n118: \n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n122: \n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n129: \n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n136: \n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n147:     gte {}\n148:   }];\n149: \n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n151:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n152:   string stat_prefix = 8;\n153: \n154:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n155:   // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n156:   // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n157:   // with the header prefix set via\n158:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n159:   // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n160:   // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n161:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n162:   // route to be recomputed, set the\n163:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n164:   // field to true in the same response.\n165:   config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n166: \n167:   // Specify the upper bound of\n168:   // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n169:   // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n170:   google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n171:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n172:     gte {}\n173:   }];\n174: \n175:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n176:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n177:   // field is set in an external processor response.\n178:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n179: \n180:   // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n181:   // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n182:   HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n183: \n184:   // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n185:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n186:   // ext_proc filter name.\n187:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n188: \n189:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n190:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n191:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n192:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n193:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n194:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n195: \n196:   // If set to true, ignore the\n197:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n198:   // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n199:   // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n200:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n201:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n202: \n203:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n204:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n205: \n206:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n207:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n208:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n209:   //\n210:   // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n211:   // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n212:   //\n213:   // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n214:   // This also means that\n215:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n216:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n217:   //\n218:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n219:   //\n220:   // .. warning::\n221:   //\n222:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n223:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n224:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n225:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n226:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n227:   //\n228:   bool observability_mode = 17;\n229: }\n230: \n231: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n232: // dynamic metadata. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n253:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n254:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n255: }\n256: \n257: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n258: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n259: //\n260: // This works as below:\n261: //\n262: //   1. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n264: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n265: //   3. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n268: //      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n269: message HeaderForwardingRules {\n270:   // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n271:   // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n272:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n273: \n274:   // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n275:   // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n276:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n277: }\n278: \n279: // Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n280: // virtual host or cluster.\n281: message ExtProcPerRoute {\n282:   oneof override {\n283:     option (validate.required) = true;\n284: \n285:     // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n286:     // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n287:     bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n288: \n289:     // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n290:     // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n291:     // flag set in a less-specific one.\n292:     ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n293:   }\n294: }\n295: \n296: // Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n297: // [#next-free-field: 8]\n298: message ExtProcOverrides {\n299:   // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n300:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n301: \n302:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n303:   // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n304:   bool async_mode = 2;\n305: \n306:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n307:   // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n308:   // ``request_attributes`` field.\n309:   repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n310: \n311:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n312:   // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n313:   // ``response_attributes`` field.\n314:   repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n315: \n316:   // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n317:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n318: \n319:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n320:   // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n321:   // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n322:   // config used. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. There is no\\n162:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n163:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\\n118:     // to true.\\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\\n120:   }\\n121: \\n122:   reserved 4;\\n123: \\n124:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n125: \\n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n127:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n129: \\n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. There is no\\n162:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n163:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n25: // External Processing Filter\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n27: \n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n29: \n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n32: //\n33: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n34: \n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n138: \n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n140:   // sent. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n290:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n291:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n292: }\n293: \n294: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n295: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n296: //\n297: // This works as below:\n298: //\n299: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n300: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n301: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n302: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n303: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n304: //   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n305: //      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n306: message HeaderForwardingRules {\n307:   // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n308:   // processing server. With this change the destructor can be called on any thread.\n7:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag ``envoy.reloadable_features.allow_slot_destroy_on_worker_threads``\n8:     to ``false``.\n9: - area: ext_proc\n10:   change: |\n11:     Adding support for\n12:     :ref:`route_cache_action <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action>`.\n13:     It specifies the route action to be taken when an external processor response is received in response to request headers.\n14: - area: http2\n15:   change: |\n16:     Changes the default value of ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_oghttp2`` to ``true``. This changes the codec used for HTTP/2\n17:     requests and responses. This behavior can be reverted by setting the feature to ``false``.\n18: - area: http3\n19:   change: |\n20:     Added a happy eyeballs feature to HTTP/3 upstream, where it assuming happy eyeballs sorting results in alternating address\n21:     families will attempt the first v4 and v6 address before giving up on HTTP/3.  This change can be reverted by setting\n22:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.http3_happy_eyeballs`` to ``false``.\n23: - area: http2\n24:   change: |\n25:     Passes HTTP/2 ``DATA`` frames through a different codec API. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting the runtime\n26:     feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_visitor_for_data`` to ``false``.\n27: - area: runtime\n28:   change: |\n29:     Rejecting invalid YAML. This has been an ``ENVOY_BUG`` linked to https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/27434\n30:     for over a year with no hard-blockers so should be Ok. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting\n31:     the runtime feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.reject_invalid_yaml`` to ``false`` but the runtime guard must be\n32:     parsed before any invalid YAML.\n33: - area: proxy_protocol\n34:   change: |\n35:     Populate typed metadata by default in proxy protocol listener. Without this fix, ``DestroyChannelOnRefused`` and\\n220:     ``CustomResolverValidAfterChannelDestruction`` unit test will break.\\n221: - area: udp\\n222:   change: |\\n223:     Fixed a bug that would cause Envoy to crash when updates to a pre-existing cluster were made (e.g. ``HostSet`` changes).\\n224: - area: ext_authz\\n225:   change: |\\n226:     Handle ``append_action`` from :ref:`external authorization service <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.auth.v3.CheckResponse>`\\n227:     that was ignored.\\n228: - area: oauth2\\n229:   change: |\\n230:     Fixed a bug that would cause Envoy to crash when receiving an Oauth callback while the Oauth upstream is unhealthy\\n231:     (e.g. due to DNS issues).\\n232: - area: http\\n233:   change: |\\n234:     Fix BalsaParser resetting state too early, guarded by\\n235:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.http1_balsa_delay_reset`` which defaults to ``true``.\\n236: - area: ext_authz\\n237:   change: |\\n238:     Set the SNI value from the requested server name if it isn't available on the connection/socket. If the input stream has\\n247:     redundant data, the decompressor will loop forever.\\n248: - area: websocket\\n249:   change: |\\n250:     Only ``101`` is considered a successful response for websocket handshake for HTTP/1.1, and Envoy as a proxy will proxy the response\\n251:     header from upstream to downstream and then close the request if other status is received. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01C6QSfBdCBgohHUxQcqKKXR","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_016towHztg6LQzsV3bgR1azw","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) Filter Migration Guide\n## v1.30.0 â†’ v1.31.0\n\n**Release Date:** July 19, 2024\n\n---\n\n## 1. Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers the upgrade path for the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from version 1.30.0 (April 2024) to version 1.31.0 (July 2024). The ext_proc filter enables external services to intercept and process HTTP traffic through a bidirectional gRPC stream.\n\nThe v1.31.0 release introduces several significant improvements to the ext_proc filter, including better control over route cache handling, enhanced error reporting, support for deferred stream closure in observability mode, and improved gRPC context propagation for tracing.\n\n**Key Headlines:**\n- New `route_cache_action` enum provides explicit control over route caching behavior\n- Timeout errors now return `504 Gateway Timeout` instead of `500 Internal Server Error`\n- Support for deferred stream closure timeout in observability mode\n- Enhanced tracing context propagation in gRPC bidirectional streams\n- Deprecation of `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean in favor of the new enum\n\n---\n\n## 2. Breaking Changes\n\n### 2.1 Route Cache Handling Redesign\n\n**Impact Level:** âš ď¸Ź **Moderate** - Requires configuration review and potential behavioral changes\n\nThe route cache clearing mechanism has been redesigned to use an explicit enum-based approach instead of a simple boolean flag.\n\n#### What Changed\n\n**v1.30.0 Configuration:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Boolean flag to disable route cache clearing\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n}\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 Configuration:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Enum-based route cache action (RECOMMENDED)\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    DEFAULT = 0;   // Clear only if ext_proc says so\n    CLEAR = 1;     // Always clear\n    RETAIN = 2;    // Never clear\n  }\n\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n\n  // Legacy boolean (still supported but marked for migration)\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n      [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Path\n\n**If you are currently using `disable_clear_route_cache: true`:**\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0 Configuration\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true  # Route cache is never cleared\n```\n\n**Upgrade to v1.31.0:**\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 Configuration (RECOMMENDED)\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**If you are currently using the default behavior (`disable_clear_route_cache` not set):**\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0 Configuration (implicit DEFAULT behavior)\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    # disable_clear_route_cache not set means: clear on ext_proc request\n```\n\n**Upgrade to v1.31.0:**\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 Configuration (RECOMMENDED)\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Clear only if ext_proc response says so\n```\n\n#### Behavior Comparison Table\n\n| Scenario | v1.30.0 Config | v1.31.0 Equivalent | Behavior |\n|----------|-----------------|-------------------|----------|\n| Default route cache handling | (not set) | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Clear cache based on ext_proc response |\n| Never clear route cache | `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Never clear cache |\n| Always clear route cache | (not supported) | `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | **NEW:** Always clear cache regardless of ext_proc response |\n\n#### Implementation Details\n\n- **Source File:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto` (lines 103-120)\n- **Proto Field:** `RouteCacheAction` enum with three values: DEFAULT (0), CLEAR (1), RETAIN (2)\n- **Deprecation Timeline:** The `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean will remain functional in v1.31.0 and subsequent releases, but using `route_cache_action` is strongly recommended\n\n#### Why This Change\n\nThe new enum-based approach provides three explicit states:\n1. **DEFAULT (0):** Follows ext_proc response directives - better for dynamic decision-making\n2. **CLEAR (1):** Always clears cache - useful for routes that require fresh decisions\n3. **RETAIN (2):** Never clears cache - useful for read-only operations or performance-sensitive paths\n\nThis is more explicit than the boolean approach and eliminates ambiguity around default behavior.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Deprecated Features\n\n### 3.1 `disable_clear_route_cache` Boolean Field\n\n**Status:** Deprecated (still functional in v1.31.0)\n\n**Deprecation Message:** Use `route_cache_action` enum instead\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field is marked with UDPA deprecation annotation `field_migrate.oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"`, indicating it will eventually migrate to a oneof grouping.\n\n**Migration Advice:**\n1. Replace `disable_clear_route_cache: true` with `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n2. Remove any explicit `disable_clear_route_cache: false` settings and use `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` instead\n3. Update any control plane configurations that generate ext_proc configs\n\n**Deprecation Timeline:**\n- v1.31.0: Both fields supported, both annotations present\n- v1.32.0+: Likely still supported, but planning should begin\n- Future: May be moved to oneof grouping or removed entirely\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Features\n\n### 4.1 Route Cache Action Enum\n\n**Status:** New - Stable and recommended\n\n**Proto Definition:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n\n    // Default behavior: clear route cache only when ext_proc response\n    // has clear_route_cache field set\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache when external processor responds\n    // with request headers, regardless of clear_route_cache setting\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Never clear the route cache, even if ext_proc sets clear_route_cache\n    // Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n\n**Case 1: Routes requiring fresh routing decisions**\n```yaml\n# Always recompute routes after ext_proc processing\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Case 2: Routes where auth decisions determine routing**\n```yaml\n# External processor makes auth decisions that affect routing\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Honor ext_proc's clear_route_cache\n```\n\n**Case 3: Read-only observation mode**\n```yaml\n# External processor only observes, never changes routes\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### 4.2 Deferred Stream Closure Timeout\n\n**Status:** New - Specifically for observability_mode\n\n**Proto Definition:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Specifies the deferred closure timeout for gRPC stream\n  // that connects to external processor. Currently, the deferred\n  // stream closure is only used in observability_mode.\n  //\n  // In observability mode, gRPC streams may be held open to the\n  // external processor longer than the lifetime of the regular client\n  // to backend stream. Envoy will eventually timeout the external\n  // processor stream according to this time limit.\n  //\n  // Default: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n  google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n\n**Example: Extended observability window**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    observability_mode: true\n    # Keep the gRPC stream open for 30 seconds after the client disconnects\n    # to allow the external processor to continue observing\n    deferred_close_timeout: \"30s\"\n```\n\n**Important Notes:**\n- Only used when `observability_mode: true`\n- Default timeout is 5 seconds if not specified\n- The external processor can still close the stream before the timeout expires\n- This feature addresses flow control concerns and external processor buffering needs\n\n**Implementation:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.proto` (lines 260-265)\n\n### 4.3 Enhanced Error Handling\n\n**Status:** New - Minor behavioral change in error responses\n\nThe error handling for timeout scenarios has been improved to be more semantically correct.\n\n**Change:**\n- **v1.30.0:** Timeout errors return `500 Internal Server Error`\n- **v1.31.0:** Timeout errors return `504 Gateway Timeout`\n\n**Rationale:**\n- `504 Gateway Timeout` is semantically correct for upstream service timeouts\n- `500 Internal Server Error` incorrectly suggests an internal Envoy issue\n- This improves observability and makes client error handling more accurate\n\n**Affected Scenarios:**\n- External processor doesn't respond within `message_timeout`\n- External processor doesn't respond within `max_message_timeout`\n- In synchronous processing mode only (no timeout in async mode)\n\n**Configuration Example:**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext-proc-cluster\n    # Set appropriate timeouts\n    message_timeout: \"200ms\"  # Default\n    max_message_timeout: \"1000ms\"  # Optional\n```\n\n**Migration Impact:**\n- If downstream clients depend on receiving `500` for ext_proc failures, they may need adjustment\n- Monitoring and alerting rules looking for `500` errors will no longer catch ext_proc timeouts\n- Update log aggregation and APM tools to monitor `504` for ext_proc failures\n\n---\n\n## 5. Configuration Updates\n\n### 5.1 Required Configuration Changes\n\nNone. All v1.30.0 configurations remain valid and functional in v1.31.0.\n\n### 5.2 Recommended Configuration Updates\n\n#### Update 1: Migrate from `disable_clear_route_cache` to `route_cache_action`\n\n**Before:**\n```yaml\nfilters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext-proc-cluster\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After:**\n```yaml\nfilters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext-proc-cluster\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n    # RECOMMENDED: Use explicit route cache action\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN  # or DEFAULT or CLEAR as appropriate\n```\n\n#### Update 2: Add Observability Mode Configuration (if using observability_mode)\n\n```yaml\nfilters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext-proc-cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n    # NEW: Control how long to keep the stream open for observations\n    deferred_close_timeout: \"5s\"  # 5 seconds (default)\n```\n\n### 5.3 Per-Route Configuration Updates\n\nNo changes required to per-route configurations. The `ExtProcPerRoute` and `ExtProcOverrides` messages remain unchanged.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Behavioral Changes\n\n### 6.1 Route Cache Action Default Behavior\n\n**Field:** `route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**Type:** `RouteCacheAction` enum\n**Default Value:** `DEFAULT` (0)\n\n**Behavior:**\n- When set to `DEFAULT`: The filter respects the `clear_route_cache` field in the external processor's response to request headers\n- When set to `CLEAR`: The filter always clears the route cache after external processing of request headers\n- When set to `RETAIN`: The filter never clears the route cache, even if the external processor requests it\n\n**Change from v1.30.0:**\n- v1.30.0 didn't have explicit CLEAR option; it was implicit in the default behavior\n- v1.30.0 had only two states via boolean: DEFAULT (route cache honored ext_proc) or RETAIN (never clear)\n\n### 6.2 Error Status Code Changes\n\n**Affected:** Timeout scenarios in ext_proc processing\n\n**Before (v1.30.0):**\n```\nHTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0):**\n```\nHTTP/1.1 504 Gateway Timeout\n```\n\n**When This Occurs:**\n- External processor doesn't respond before `message_timeout` expires\n- In synchronous processing mode (not observability_mode)\n- Only affects downstream error responses; upstream timeout handling unchanged\n\n**Impact Areas:**\n- Client-side error handling\n- Monitoring and alerting\n- Logs and tracing spans\n- Custom error pages/responses\n\n### 6.3 gRPC Tracing Context Propagation\n\n**Status:** Improved in v1.31.0\n\n**Change:** Tracing context headers are now properly propagated in bidirectional gRPC streams when using ext_proc.\n\n**Affected Clients:**\n- Envoy gRPC client (via `config.core.v3.GrpcService.envoy_grpc`)\n- Google C++ gRPC client (via `config.core.v3.GrpcService.google_grpc`)\n\n**Benefits:**\n- Distributed tracing works correctly with ext_proc\n- OpenTelemetry and Jaeger integrations improved\n- Better observability for ext_proc request/response timing\n\n**Configuration Impact:**\n- No changes needed; this works automatically\n- Tracing spans will now show correct parent-child relationships with ext_proc calls\n\n---\n\n## 7. Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Review Current Configuration\n\n```bash\n# Examine all ext_proc filter configurations\ngrep -r \"ext_proc\" /path/to/config\n\n# Check for uses of disable_clear_route_cache\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /path/to/config\n```\n\n### Step 2: Plan Route Cache Migration\n\nFor each ext_proc filter configuration:\n\n| Current Setting | Migration Path | New Setting |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | Keep as-is or upgrade | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` | Keep as-is or upgrade | Remove field, use implicit DEFAULT |\n| Not specified (implicit DEFAULT) | Keep as-is or upgrade | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` |\n\n### Step 3: Update Monitoring and Alerting\n\nUpdate any monitoring rules that check for `500 Internal Server Error`:\n\n```yaml\n# OLD: Catch all 500 errors including ext_proc timeouts\n- alert: HighErrorRate\n  expr: rate(envoy_http_requests_total{response_code=\"500\"}[5m]) > 0.05\n\n# NEW: Separate concerns\n- alert: ExtProcTimeout\n  expr: rate(envoy_http_requests_total{response_code=\"504\"}[5m]) > 0.05\n- alert: OtherServerErrors\n  expr: rate(envoy_http_requests_total{response_code=\"500\"}[5m]) > 0.05\n```\n\n### Step 4: Update Logging and Analysis\n\nIf you have custom log parsing or analysis:\n\n```\n# v1.30.0 logs for ext_proc timeout\n[2024-04-15 10:23:45] ERROR ext_proc timeout -> HTTP 500\n\n# v1.31.0 logs for ext_proc timeout\n[2024-07-19 10:23:45] ERROR ext_proc timeout -> HTTP 504\n```\n\n### Step 5: Stage Deployment\n\n**Phase 1: Development/Staging**\n1. Deploy v1.31.0 Envoy binaries\n2. Keep all ext_proc configs unchanged (backward compatible)\n3. Verify ext_proc functionality with existing configs\n4. Test error handling with intentional timeouts\n\n**Phase 2: Production Canary**\n1. Route 5-10% of production traffic through v1.31.0\n2. Monitor error rates, latencies, and 504 vs 500 error distribution\n3. Verify that `504` errors are only ext_proc timeouts\n4. Validate downstream client error handling\n\n**Phase 3: Gradual Rollout**\n1. Gradually increase traffic through v1.31.0\n2. Update config for `route_cache_action` on non-critical routes\n3. Validate route caching behavior changes\n4. Monitor for any unexpected interactions\n\n**Phase 4: Update Configuration**\n1. Update all ext_proc configs to use `route_cache_action`\n2. Remove `disable_clear_route_cache` from configs\n3. Add `deferred_close_timeout` if using `observability_mode`\n4. Complete rollout to 100%\n\n### Step 6: Configuration Examples\n\n**Example 1: Basic Auth Service (DEFAULT route cache handling)**\n```yaml\n# Before\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: auth-processor\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n\n# After (optional, uses default behavior)\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: auth-processor\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n    route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n**Example 2: Read-Only Logging Service (RETAIN route cache)**\n```yaml\n# Before\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: log-processor\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n    observability_mode: true\n\n# After\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: log-processor\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN\n    observability_mode: true\n    deferred_close_timeout: \"5s\"\n```\n\n**Example 3: Authorization Service with Dynamic Routes (CLEAR route cache)**\n```yaml\n# NEW in v1.31.0 - Not possible in v1.30.0\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: auth-processor\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n    # Always recompute routes after auth decisions\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    # Modify headers based on auth outcome\n    mutation_rules:\n      allow_all_headers: false\n      allow_envoy_headers: false\n      allowed_headers:\n        patterns:\n        - exact: \"x-user-id\"\n        - exact: \"x-user-role\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## 8. Testing Recommendations\n\n### 8.1 Unit Testing\n\n**Test Case 1: Route Cache Action Behavior**\n```go\n// Test DEFAULT: cache cleared only if ext_proc says so\nfunc TestRouteCacheActionDefault() {\n    // Configure route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n    // Send ext_proc response with clear_route_cache: true\n    // Assert: route cache was cleared\n\n    // Send ext_proc response with clear_route_cache: false\n    // Assert: route cache was NOT cleared\n}\n\n// Test CLEAR: cache always cleared\nfunc TestRouteCacheActionClear() {\n    // Configure route_cache_action: CLEAR\n    // Send ext_proc response with clear_route_cache: false\n    // Assert: route cache was cleared anyway\n}\n\n// Test RETAIN: cache never cleared\nfunc TestRouteCacheActionRetain() {\n    // Configure route_cache_action: RETAIN\n    // Send ext_proc response with clear_route_cache: true\n    // Assert: route cache was NOT cleared\n}\n```\n\n**Test Case 2: Error Status Codes**\n```go\nfunc TestExtProcTimeoutReturns504() {\n    // Configure message_timeout: 100ms\n    // Don't respond from ext_proc\n    // Assert: Returns HTTP 504\n    // Assert: NOT HTTP 500\n}\n```\n\n### 8.2 Integration Testing\n\n**Test Scenario 1: Backward Compatibility**\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0 config should work unchanged in v1.31.0\n---\napiVersion: v1\nkind: ConfigMap\nmetadata:\n  name: envoy-config-v130\ndata:\n  envoy.yaml: |\n    http_filters:\n    -
